## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force (e.g., Duffing), in the damping (e.g., van der Pol), or through external time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubic damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * v**2 (coupled position-velocity nonlinearity)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x**2 (general nonlinear expansion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric double-well or hardening/softening potential
- Terms of form (1 - c*x²)*v → self-excited oscillation with amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycles)
- Cosine or sine of c*t as additive terms → external periodic driving force
- Product terms x*v or x²*v → energy-dependent coupling between position and velocity
- Cubic position term with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x - c1*x³) → double-well Duffing potential
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v³) → dissipative forces preserving time-reversal symmetry structure
- Position multiplied by trigonometric function of time → parametric excitation / Mathieu-type dynamics
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, energy conservation or dissipation only
- Even powers of x multiplying v → amplitude-dependent damping that preserves oscillation symmetry
- Ratio of polynomial in x over (1 + c*x²) → bounded nonlinear restoring force with saturation

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
`-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v + 0.332588*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Combining v³ terms: `(0.332588 - 0.0589613)*v³ = 0.273627*v³`

So GT = `0.385230*sin(t) - 0.332588*v + 0.273627*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|)`

The key challenge is the `exp(-|x|)` term. Most candidates have `exp(c*x)`, which is `exp(cx)`, not `exp(-|x|)`. The function `exp(-|x|)` is not the same as `exp(cx)` for any constant c, because `exp(-|x|)` is symmetric and has a kink at x=0, while `exp(cx)` is smooth and monotonic.

Let me check each candidate for structural compatibility:

**Candidates with `v*exp(c*x)` terms** (most candidates): These cannot match `v*exp(-|x|)` because `exp(cx)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)` for any constant c. This eliminates candidates 1-31, 41, 46, 48, 49.

**Candidate 32:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*sin(c4*x+c5*v+c6) + c7*v*exp(c8*x) + c9*v³` - Has sin of mixed terms and exp(cx), can't match.

**Candidate 33:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*sin(c4+c5*v) + c6*v + c7*v*exp(c8*x)` - Missing v³, has sin(v), can't match.

**Candidate 34:** `c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c4*v³ + c5*v*x^c6 + c7*v*log(c8*x²+1)` - Has `v*log(c8*x²+1)`. Note that `log(c8*x²+1)` is symmetric in x. But can it equal `c*exp(-|x|) + d*v` for some rearrangement? No, log and exp are different functions.

**Candidate 37-39, 43:** Have `v*x^c` terms. Setting c to specific values gives power functions, not exp(-|x|).

**Candidate 40, 44, 45, 47:** Have `c3*exp(c4*x²)` terms. Note `exp(-x²)` is symmetric like `exp(-|x|)` but they're different functions. Also these have `v*x` not `v*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 42:** `c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c4*x + c5*v + c6*v³ + c7*v*log(c8*x²+1)`. The term `v*log(c8*x²+1)` is symmetric in x. But `log(c*x²+1)` ≠ `k*exp(-|x|)` for any constants.

**Candidate 50:** `c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c4*x + c5*v + c6*v³ + c7*x/(c8*x²+1) + c9*v*x` - Has `v*x` which is odd, but `v*exp(-|x|)` is even in x. Can't match.

**Candidate 35, 36, 38:** Various power/rational terms, none can produce exp(-|x|).

None of the candidates contain a term that can reproduce `exp(-|x|)` or any equivalent symmetric exponential decay. The `exp(c*x)` term in most candidates is fundamentally different from `exp(-|x|)` - it's smooth and monotonic vs. having a cusp at x=0 and being symmetric.

After careful analysis, no candidate can match the GT because none can reproduce the `exp(-|x|)` dependence.
